<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Bee Gees</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">

<p>The <b>Bee Gees</b> were a pop music group formed in 1958. The group's line-up consisted of brothers <a href="/wiki/Barry_Gibb" title="Barry Gibb">Barry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robin_Gibb" title="Robin Gibb">Robin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maurice_Gibb" title="Maurice Gibb">Maurice Gibb</a>. The trio were successful for most of their decades of recording music, but they had two distinct periods of exceptional success: as a rock act in the late 1960s and early 1970s, and as prominent performers of the <a href="/wiki/Disco" title="Disco">disco</a> music era in the late 1970s. The group sang recognisable three-part <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Close_harmony" title="Close harmony">tight harmonies</a>; Robin's clear <a href="/wiki/Vibrato" title="Vibrato">vibrato</a> lead vocals were a hallmark of their earlier hits, while Barry's <a href="/wiki/Rhythm_and_blues" title="Rhythm and blues">R&amp;B</a> <a href="/wiki/Falsetto" title="Falsetto">falsetto</a> became their signature sound during the late 1970s and 1980s. They wrote all of their own hits, as well as writing and producing several major hits for other artists.</p>
<p>Born on the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man" title="Isle of Man">Isle of Man</a> to English parents, the Gibb brothers lived in <a href="/wiki/Chorlton-cum-Hardy" title="Chorlton-cum-Hardy">Chorlton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a>, England, until the late 1950s, and formed the <a href="/wiki/The_Rattlesnakes_(1955_band)" title="The Rattlesnakes (1955 band)">Rattlesnakes</a>. The family then moved to <a href="/wiki/Redcliffe,_Queensland" title="Redcliffe, Queensland">Redcliffe</a>, in Queensland, Australia, and then to <a href="/wiki/Cribb_Island,_Queensland" title="Cribb Island, Queensland">Cribb Island</a>. After achieving their first chart success in Australia as the Bee Gees with "<a href="/wiki/Spicks_and_Specks_(song)" title="Spicks and Specks (song)">Spicks and Specks</a>" (their 12th single), they returned to the UK in January 1967 where producer <a href="/wiki/Robert_Stigwood" title="Robert Stigwood">Robert Stigwood</a> began promoting them to a worldwide audience.</p>
<p>The Bee Gees have sold more than 220 million records worldwide, making them one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_music_artists" title="List of best-selling music artists">world's best-selling music artists</a> of all time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardianjuly13_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-Guardianjuly13-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> They were inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a> in 1997;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HoF_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-HoF-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> the presenter of the award to "Britain's first family of harmony" was <a href="/wiki/Brian_Wilson" title="Brian Wilson">Brian Wilson</a>, historical leader of <a href="/wiki/The_Beach_Boys" title="The Beach Boys">the Beach Boys</a>, a "family act" also featuring three harmonising brothers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reason_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-reason-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> The Bee Gees' <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hall_of_Fame" title="Hall of Fame">Hall of Fame</a> citation says "Only <a href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley" title="Elvis Presley">Elvis Presley</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">the Beatles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Garth_Brooks" title="Garth Brooks">Garth Brooks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paul_McCartney" title="Paul McCartney">Paul McCartney</a> have outsold the Bee Gees."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Following Maurice's sudden death in January 2003 at the age of 53, Barry and Robin retired the group's name after 45 years of activity. In 2009 Robin announced that he and Barry had agreed that the Bee Gees would re-form and perform again.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> Robin died in May 2012 at the age of 62, after a prolonged struggle with cancer and other health problems, leaving Barry as the lone surviving member of the group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p></p>

Plaque at Maitland Terrace/Strang Road intersection in Union Mills, <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man" title="Isle of Man">Isle of Man</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1955, <a href="/wiki/Barry_Gibb" title="Barry Gibb">Barry Gibb</a> along with his brothers <a href="/wiki/Robin_Gibb" title="Robin Gibb">Robin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maurice_Gibb" title="Maurice Gibb">Maurice Gibb</a> moved back to their father <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Gibb" title="Hugh Gibb">Hugh Gibb</a>'s home town of <a href="/wiki/Chorlton-cum-Hardy" title="Chorlton-cum-Hardy">Chorlton-cum-Hardy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a>, England where they went to Oswald Road Primary School,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-robinmail_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-robinmail-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> and they formed a <a href="/wiki/Skiffle" title="Skiffle">skiffle</a>/rock-and-roll group the <a href="/wiki/The_Rattlesnakes_(1955_band)" title="The Rattlesnakes (1955 band)">Rattlesnakes</a>, which consisted of Barry on guitar and vocals, Robin and Maurice on vocals, with friends Paul Frost on drums and Kenny Horrocks on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tea-chest_bass" title="Tea-chest bass">tea-chest bass</a>. In December 1957 the boys began to sing in harmony. The story is told that they were going to <a href="/wiki/Lip_sync" title="Lip sync">lip sync</a> to a record in the local Gaumont cinema (as other children had done on previous weeks) and as they were running to the theatre, the fragile shellac 78-RPM record broke. The brothers had to sing live and received such a positive response from the audience that they decided to pursue a singing career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-robinmail_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-robinmail-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Storyabout-pt2_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Storyabout-pt2-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> In May 1958 the Rattlesnakes were disbanded when Frost and Horrocks left to form Wee Johnny Hayes and the Blue Cats.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-were_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-were-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In August 1958 the Gibb family, including older sister Lesley and infant brother <a href="/wiki/Andy_Gibb" title="Andy Gibb">Andy</a>, emigrated to <a href="/wiki/Redcliffe,_Queensland" title="Redcliffe, Queensland">Redcliffe</a>, just north-east of <a href="/wiki/Brisbane" title="Brisbane">Brisbane</a> in <a href="/wiki/Queensland" title="Queensland">Queensland</a>, Australia. The young brothers attended Humpybong State School<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-robinmail_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-robinmail-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> and began performing to raise <a href="/wiki/Allowance_(money)#Allowances_for_children" title="Allowance (money)">pocket money</a>. They were introduced to leading Brisbane radio DJ Bill Gates by <a href="/wiki/Dirt_track_racing" title="Dirt track racing">speedway</a> promoter and driver Bill Goode, who had hired the brothers to entertain the crowd at the Redcliffe Speedway in 1960. Gates renamed them the BG's (later changed to "Bee Gees") after his, Goode's, and Barry Gibb's initials—thus the name was not specifically a reference to "Brothers Gibb", despite popular belief.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> The family relocated to Cribb Island which was later demolished for Brisbane Airport. While there the brothers went to Northgate State School.</p>
<p>By 1960 the Bee Gees were featured on television shows including their performance of "Time Is Passing By".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> In the next few years they began working regularly at resorts on the Queensland coast. For his songwriting, Barry sparked the interest of Australian star <a href="/wiki/Col_Joye" title="Col Joye">Col Joye</a>, who helped them get a record deal in 1963 with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Festival_Records_(Australia)" title="Festival Records (Australia)">Festival Records</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-robinmail_8-3"><a href="#cite_note-robinmail-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> subsidiary <a href="/wiki/Leedon_Records" title="Leedon Records">Leedon Records</a> under the name "Bee Gees". The three released two or three singles a year, while Barry supplied additional songs to other Australian artists. In 1962, the Bee Gees were chosen as the supporting act for <a href="/wiki/Chubby_Checker" title="Chubby Checker">Chubby Checker</a>'s concert in Sydney Stadium.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> From 1963 to 1966 the Gibb family lived at 171 Bunnerong Road, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maroubra" title="Maroubra">Maroubra</a> in Sydney.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> Robin Gibb recorded the song "Sydney", about the brothers' experience living in Sydney, just prior to his death. It was released on his posthumous album <i>50 St. Catherine's Drive</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> A minor hit in 1965, "<a href="/wiki/Wine_and_Women" title="Wine and Women">Wine and Women</a>", led to the group's first LP <i><a href="/wiki/The_Bee_Gees_Sing_and_Play_14_Barry_Gibb_Songs" title="The Bee Gees Sing and Play 14 Barry Gibb Songs">The Bee Gees Sing and Play 14 Barry Gibb Songs</a></i>. By 1966 Festival was, however, on the verge of dropping them from the Leedon roster because of their perceived lack of commercial success. It was at this time that they met American-born songwriter, producer and entrepreneur, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Nat_Kipner&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Nat Kipner (page does not exist)">Nat Kipner</a>, who had just been appointed A&amp;R manager of a new independent label, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spin_Records_(Australian_Label)" title="Spin Records (Australian Label)">Spin Records</a>. Kipner briefly took over as the group's manager and successfully negotiated their transfer to Spin in exchange for Festival being granted the Australian distribution rights to the group's recordings.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Through Kipner the Bee Gees met engineer-producer, <a href="/wiki/Ossie_Byrne" title="Ossie Byrne">Ossie Byrne</a>. He produced (or co-produced with Kipner) many of the earlier Spin recordings, most of which were cut at his own small self-built St Clair Studio in the Sydney suburb of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurstville" title="Hurstville">Hurstville</a>. Byrne gave the Gibb brothers virtually unlimited access to St Clair Studio over a period of several months in mid-1966.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> The group later acknowledged that this enabled them to greatly improve their skills as recording artists. During this productive time they recorded a large batch of original material—including the song that would become their first major hit, "<a href="/wiki/Spicks_and_Specks_(song)" title="Spicks and Specks (song)">Spicks and Specks</a>" (on which Byrne played the trumpet coda)—as well as cover versions of current hits by overseas acts such as The Beatles. They regularly collaborated with other local musicians, including members of beat band Steve &amp; The Board, led by <a href="/wiki/Steve_Kipner" title="Steve Kipner">Steve Kipner</a>, Nat's teenage son.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Frustrated by their lack of success, the Gibbs decided to return to England in late 1966. Ossie Byrne travelled with them, and Colin Petersen, who eventually became the group's drummer, followed soon after. While at sea in January 1967, they learned that "Spicks and Specks" had been awarded Best Single of the Year by <i><a href="/wiki/Go-Set" title="Go-Set">Go-Set</a></i>, Australia's most popular and influential music newspaper.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1967.E2.80.9368:_International_fame_and_touring_years">1967–68: International fame and touring years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bee_Gees&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1967–68: International fame and touring years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Bee_Gees.27_1st.2C_Horizontal.2C_and_Idea"><i>Bee Gees' 1st</i>, <i>Horizontal</i>, and <i>Idea</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bee_Gees&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Bee Gees' 1st, Horizontal, and Idea">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/The_Bee_Gees%27_concerts_in_1967_and_1968" title="The Bee Gees' concerts in 1967 and 1968">The Bee Gees' concerts in 1967 and 1968</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bee_gees_1970.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="503" data-file-width="752" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Bee_gees_1970.JPG/250px-Bee_gees_1970.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Bee_gees_1970.JPG/375px-Bee_gees_1970.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Bee_gees_1970.JPG/500px-Bee_gees_1970.JPG 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bee_gees_1970.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Bee Gees in 1967 (left to right: Barry Gibb, Robin Gibb, Vince Melouney, Maurice Gibb, and Colin Petersen)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Before their departure from Australia to England, Hugh Gibb sent demos to <a href="/wiki/Brian_Epstein" title="Brian Epstein">Brian Epstein</a>, a promoter who managed <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">The Beatles</a> and directed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NEMS_Enterprises" title="NEMS Enterprises">NEMS</a>, a British music store. Brian Epstein passed the demo tapes to <a href="/wiki/Robert_Stigwood" title="Robert Stigwood">Robert Stigwood</a>, who had recently joined NEMS.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> After an audition with Stigwood in February 1967, The Bee Gees signed a five-year contract whereby <a href="/wiki/Polydor_Records" title="Polydor Records">Polydor Records</a> would release their records in the UK and <a href="/wiki/Atco_Records" title="Atco Records">Atco Records</a> would do so in the US. Work quickly began on the group's first international album, and Stigwood launched a promotional campaign to coincide with its release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Stigwood proclaimed that the Bee Gees were "The Most Significant New Talent of 1967", thus initiating the comparison of The Bee Gees to The Beatles. Before recording the first album they added <a href="/wiki/Colin_Petersen" title="Colin Petersen">Colin Petersen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vince_Melouney" title="Vince Melouney">Vince Melouney</a> to make the group as a band.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pc49_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-pc49-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/New_York_Mining_Disaster_1941" title="New York Mining Disaster 1941">New York Mining Disaster 1941</a>", their second British single (their first-issued UK 45 <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_per_minute" title="Revolutions per minute">rpm</a> was "Spicks and Specks"), was issued to radio stations with a blank white label listing only the song title. Some DJs immediately assumed this was a new single by The Beatles and started playing the song in <a href="/wiki/Rotation_(music)" title="Rotation (music)">heavy rotation</a>. This helped the song climb into the top 20 in both the UK and US. No such chicanery was needed to boost The Bee Gees' second single, "<a href="/wiki/To_Love_Somebody_(song)" title="To Love Somebody (song)">To Love Somebody</a>", into the US Top 20. Originally written for <a href="/wiki/Otis_Redding" title="Otis Redding">Otis Redding</a>, "To Love Somebody", a soulful ballad sung by Barry, has since become a pop standard covered by many artists including <a href="/wiki/The_Flying_Burrito_Brothers" title="The Flying Burrito Brothers">The Flying Burrito Brothers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rod_Stewart" title="Rod Stewart">Rod Stewart</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bonnie_Tyler" title="Bonnie Tyler">Bonnie Tyler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Janis_Joplin" title="Janis Joplin">Janis Joplin</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Animals" title="The Animals">The Animals</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gary_Puckett_and_the_Union_Gap" title="Gary Puckett and the Union Gap">Gary Puckett and the Union Gap</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nina_Simone" title="Nina Simone">Nina Simone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Somerville" title="Jimmy Somerville">Jimmy Somerville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Billy_Corgan" title="Billy Corgan">Billy Corgan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Michael_Bolton" title="Michael Bolton">Michael Bolton</a>. Another single, "<a href="/wiki/Holiday_(Bee_Gees_song)" title="Holiday (Bee Gees song)">Holiday</a>", was released in the US, peaking at No. 16. The parent album, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bee_Gees_1st" title="Bee Gees 1st">Bee Gees 1st</a></i> (their first internationally), peaked at No. 7 in the US and No. 8 in the UK. Bill Shepherd was credited as the arranger. After recording that album, the band recorded their first BBC session at the <a href="/wiki/Playhouse_Theatre" title="Playhouse Theatre">Playhouse Theatre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northumberland_Avenue" title="Northumberland Avenue">Northumberland Avenue</a>, in London, with Bill Bebb as the producer, and they performed three songs. That session is included on <i>BBC Sessions: 1967–1973</i> (2008).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> Following the release of <i>Bee Gees' 1st</i>, the band was first introduced in New York as "the English surprise".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>At that time, the band made their first British TV appearance on <i><a href="/wiki/Top_of_the_Pops" title="Top of the Pops">Top of the Pops</a></i> as Maurice recalled:</p>
<table class="cquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;"><a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Savile" title="Jimmy Savile">Jimmy Savile</a> was on it and that was amazing because we'd seen pictures of him in The Beatles fan club book, so we thought we were really there! That show had <a href="/wiki/Lulu_(singer)" title="Lulu (singer)">Lulu</a>, us, <a href="/wiki/The_Move" title="The Move">The Move</a>, and <a href="/wiki/The_Rolling_Stones" title="The Rolling Stones">The [Rolling] Stones</a> doing '<a href="/wiki/Let%27s_Spend_the_Night_Together" title="Let's Spend the Night Together">Let's Spend the Night Together</a>'. You have to remember this was really before the superstar was invented so you were all in it together.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBilyeuCookHughes2009_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBilyeuCookHughes2009-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The three-part Gibb harmony was compared to The Beatles, although Bee Gees fans familiar with the voices have not always agreed. On 31 December 1967, the band finished the year off with their Christmas Eve special <i>How on Earth?</i> Ten days earlier, at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liverpool_Anglican_Cathedral" title="Liverpool Anglican Cathedral">Liverpool Anglican Cathedral</a>, the program was broadcast at 6:35 PM and they performed their own song "Thank You For Christmas" (which was recorded in the <i>Horizontal</i> sessions but was not released until 2008) and also "<a href="/wiki/Silent_Night" title="Silent Night">Silent Night</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Hark!_The_Herald_Angels_Sing" title="Hark! The Herald Angels Sing">Hark! The Herald Angels Sing</a>". The folk group <a href="/wiki/The_Settlers" title="The Settlers">The Settlers</a> also performed on the same program and were conducted by The Very Reverend Edward H. Patey, Dean of the Cathedral.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBilyeuCookHughes2009_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBilyeuCookHughes2009-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In late 1967, they began recording for the second album. January 1968 began with a promotional trip to the US. The <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Police_Department" title="Los Angeles Police Department">Los Angeles Police Department</a> was on alert in anticipation of a Beatles-type reception and special security arrangements were being put in place.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pc49_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-pc49-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> In February, <i><a href="/wiki/Horizontal_(album)" title="Horizontal (album)">Horizontal</a></i> repeated the success of their first album, featuring their first UK No. 1 single "<a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_(Bee_Gees_song)" title="Massachusetts (Bee Gees song)">Massachusetts</a>" (a No. 11 US hit), and the No. 7 UK single "<a href="/wiki/World_(Bee_Gees_song)" title="World (Bee Gees song)">World</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Charts_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-Charts-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> The sound of the album <i>Horizontal</i> had a more "rock" sound than their previous release, though ballads like "<a href="/wiki/And_the_Sun_Will_Shine" title="And the Sun Will Shine">And the Sun Will Shine</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Really_and_Sincerely" title="Really and Sincerely">Really and Sincerely</a>" were also prominent. The <i>Horizontal</i> album reached No. 12 in the US, and No. 16 in the UK. Promoting the record, the band made their first appearance on US television on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Smothers_Brothers_Show" title="The Smothers Brothers Show">The Smothers Brothers Show</a></i> on CBS. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tommy_Smothers" title="Tommy Smothers">Tommy Smothers</a> had first encountered the band on a trip to London, and became their friend as well as a fan. That evening, Tommy wore a shirt which Maurice had bought for him at The Beatles' <a href="/wiki/Apple_Boutique" title="Apple Boutique">Apple Boutique</a>. With the release of <i>Horizontal</i>, they also embarked on a Scandinavian tour with concerts in <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a>. On 27 February 1968, the band, backed by the 17-piece Massachusetts String Orchestra, began their first tour of Germany with two concerts at Hamburg Musikhalle. The band was supported by <a href="/wiki/Procol_Harum" title="Procol Harum">Procol Harum</a> (who had a well-known hit "<a href="/wiki/A_Whiter_Shade_of_Pale" title="A Whiter Shade of Pale">A Whiter Shade of Pale</a>") on their German tour in March 1968.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> As Robin's partner Molly Hullis recalls: "Germans were wilder than the fans in England at the heights of <a href="/wiki/Beatlemania" title="Beatlemania">Beatlemania</a>." The tour schedule took them to 11 venues in as many days with 18 concerts played, finishing with a brace of shows at the Braunschewig Stadhalle. After that, the group was off to Switzerland. As Maurice described it,</p>
<table class="cquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">There were over 5,000 kids at the airport in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zurich" title="Zurich">Zurich</a>. The entire ride to <a href="/wiki/Bern" title="Bern">Bern</a>, the kids were waving <a href="/wiki/Union_Jack" title="Union Jack">Union Jacks</a>. When we got to the hotel, the police weren't there to meet us and the kids crushed the car. We were inside and the windows were all getting smashed in, and we were on the floor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBilyeuCookHughes2009_23-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBilyeuCookHughes2009-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>On 17 March, the band performed on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Ed_Sullivan_Show" title="The Ed Sullivan Show">The Ed Sullivan Show</a></i> performing "Words". The other artists who performed on the same day are <a href="/wiki/Lucille_Ball" title="Lucille Ball">Lucille Ball</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Hamilton_(actor)" title="George Hamilton (actor)">George Hamilton</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fran_Jeffries" title="Fran Jeffries">Fran Jeffries</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> On 27 March 1968, the band performed at the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Albert_Hall" title="Royal Albert Hall">Royal Albert Hall</a> in London.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBilyeuCookHughes2009_23-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBilyeuCookHughes2009-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Bee_Gees.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="502" data-file-width="500" height="221" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/The_Bee_Gees.png/220px-The_Bee_Gees.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/The_Bee_Gees.png/330px-The_Bee_Gees.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/The_Bee_Gees.png/440px-The_Bee_Gees.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Bee_Gees.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Bee Gees performing on Dutch television <i>Twien</i> in 1968</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Two more singles followed in early 1968, the ballad "<a href="/wiki/Words_(Bee_Gees_song)" title="Words (Bee Gees song)">Words</a>" (No. 8 UK, No. 15 US) and the double A-sided single "<a href="/wiki/Jumbo_(Bee_Gees_song)" title="Jumbo (Bee Gees song)">Jumbo</a>" b/w "<a href="/wiki/The_Singer_Sang_His_Song" title="The Singer Sang His Song">The Singer Sang His Song</a>". "Jumbo" was the Bee Gees' least successful single to date only reaching No. 25 in the UK and No. 57 in the US. The Bee Gees felt that "The Singer Sang His Song" was the stronger of the two sides, an opinion shared by listeners in the Netherlands who made it a No. 3 hit. Further Bee Gees chart singles followed: "<a href="/wiki/I%27ve_Gotta_Get_a_Message_to_You" title="I've Gotta Get a Message to You">I've Gotta Get a Message to You</a>", their second UK No. 1 (No. 8 US) and "<a href="/wiki/I_Started_a_Joke" title="I Started a Joke">I Started a Joke</a>" (No. 6 US), both culled from the band's third album <i><a href="/wiki/Idea_(album)" title="Idea (album)">Idea</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Charts_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-Charts-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Idea</i> reached No. 4 in the UK and was another top 20 album in the US (No. 17).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Charts_24-2"><a href="#cite_note-Charts-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> Following the tour and TV special to promote the album, Vince Melouney left the group, feeling that he wanted to play more of a blues style music than the Gibbs were writing. Melouney did achieve one feat while with the Bee Gees – his composition "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Such_a_Shame_(Bee_Gees_song)" title="Such a Shame (Bee Gees song)">Such a Shame</a>" (from <i>Idea</i>) is the only song on any Bee Gees album not written by a Gibb brother. The group also filmed a BBC television special with <a href="/wiki/Frankie_Howerd" title="Frankie Howerd">Frankie Howerd</a> called <i>Frankie Howerd Meets The Bee Gees</i>, written by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ray_Galton" title="Ray Galton">Ray Galton</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alan_Simpson_(scriptwriter)" title="Alan Simpson (scriptwriter)">Alan Simpson</a>. This gave the group the opportunity to show their own comedy skills in sketches with Howerd. The band were due to begin a seven-week tour of the US on 2 August 1968, but on 27 July, Robin collapsed and fell unconscious. He was admitted to a London nursing home suffering from nervous exhaustion and the American tour was postponed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBilyeuCookHughes2009_23-4"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBilyeuCookHughes2009-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> The band started to record their sixth album and this resulted in spending a week recording at <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Studios" title="Atlantic Studios">Atlantic Studios</a> in New York. Robin, not feeling well, missed the New York sessions, but the rest of the band put away instrumental tracks and demos.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Odessa.2C_Cucumber_Castle_and_break-up"><i>Odessa</i>, <i>Cucumber Castle</i> and break-up</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bee_Gees&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Odessa, Cucumber Castle and break-up">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Bee_Gees_-_This_is_Tom_Jones,_Season_1,_Episode_3_(1969).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="653" data-file-width="834" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/The_Bee_Gees_-_This_is_Tom_Jones%2C_Season_1%2C_Episode_3_%281969%29.jpg/220px-The_Bee_Gees_-_This_is_Tom_Jones%2C_Season_1%2C_Episode_3_%281969%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/The_Bee_Gees_-_This_is_Tom_Jones%2C_Season_1%2C_Episode_3_%281969%29.jpg/330px-The_Bee_Gees_-_This_is_Tom_Jones%2C_Season_1%2C_Episode_3_%281969%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/The_Bee_Gees_-_This_is_Tom_Jones%2C_Season_1%2C_Episode_3_%281969%29.jpg/440px-The_Bee_Gees_-_This_is_Tom_Jones%2C_Season_1%2C_Episode_3_%281969%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Bee_Gees_-_This_is_Tom_Jones,_Season_1,_Episode_3_(1969).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Bee Gees performing at <i><a href="/wiki/This_Is_Tom_Jones" title="This Is Tom Jones">The Tom Jones Show</a></i> in early 1969, one of the last performance with Robin as he left the group later in March.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>By 1969, the cracks started to show within the group as Robin began to feel that Stigwood had been favouring Barry as the frontman. Their next album, which was to have been a concept album called <i>Masterpeace</i>, evolved into the double-album <i><a href="/wiki/Odessa_(Bee_Gees_album)" title="Odessa (Bee Gees album)">Odessa</a></i>. Most rock critics felt this was the best Bee Gees album of the 1960s with its progressive rock feel on the <a href="/wiki/Odessa_(City_on_the_Black_Sea)" title="Odessa (City on the Black Sea)">title track</a>, the country-flavoured "<a href="/wiki/Marley_Purt_Drive" title="Marley Purt Drive">Marley Purt Drive</a>" and "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Give_Your_Best" title="Give Your Best">Give Your Best</a>", and ballads such as "<a href="/wiki/Melody_Fair" title="Melody Fair">Melody Fair</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/First_of_May_(Bee_Gees_song)" title="First of May (Bee Gees song)">First of May</a>"; (the last of which became the only single from the album and was a minor hit). Feeling that the flipside, "<a href="/wiki/Lamplight" title="Lamplight">Lamplight</a>" should have been the A-side, Robin quit the group in mid-1969 and launched a solo career, seeing brief success in Europe with his No. 2 hit "<a href="/wiki/Saved_by_the_Bell_(song)" title="Saved by the Bell (song)">Saved by the Bell</a>" and the album <i><a href="/wiki/Robin%27s_Reign" title="Robin's Reign">Robin's Reign</a></i>. The first of many Bee Gees compilations, <i><a href="/wiki/Best_of_Bee_Gees" title="Best of Bee Gees">Best of Bee Gees</a></i>, was released featuring the non-LP single "<a href="/wiki/Words_(Bee_Gees_song)" title="Words (Bee Gees song)">Words</a>" plus the Australian hit "<a href="/wiki/Spicks_and_Specks_(song)" title="Spicks and Specks (song)">Spicks and Specks</a>". The single "<a href="/wiki/Tomorrow_Tomorrow_(Bee_Gees_song)" title="Tomorrow Tomorrow (Bee Gees song)">Tomorrow Tomorrow</a>" was also released and was a moderate hit in the UK reaching No. 23, but only No. 54 in the US. The compilation reached the top ten in both the UK and the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Charts_24-3"><a href="#cite_note-Charts-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> The Bee Gees' performances in early 1969 on the <i><a href="/wiki/Top_of_the_Pops" title="Top of the Pops">Top of the Pops</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/This_Is_Tom_Jones" title="This Is Tom Jones">The Tom Jones Show</a></i> performing "I Started a Joke" and "First of May" as a medley was one of the last live performances of the group with Robin before he announces his break-up in March 19.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>While Robin pursued his solo career, Barry, Maurice, and Petersen continued on as the Bee Gees recording their next album, <i><a href="/wiki/Cucumber_Castle" title="Cucumber Castle">Cucumber Castle</a></i>. The band made their debut performance without Robin at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Talk_of_the_Town_(nightclub)" title="Talk of the Town (nightclub)">Talk of the Town</a>. They had recruited their sister, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Lesley_Evans&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Lesley Evans (page does not exist)">Lesley</a>, into the group at this time. There was also a TV special filmed to accompany the album which aired on the BBC in 1971. Petersen played drums on the tracks recorded for the album, but was fired from the group after filming began. His parts were edited out of the final cut of the film. After Petersen was fired, he formed the <a href="/wiki/Humpy_Bong" title="Humpy Bong">Humpy Bong</a> with <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Kelly" title="Jonathan Kelly">Jonathan Kelly</a>. <a href="/wiki/Pentangle_(band)" title="Pentangle (band)">Pentangle</a> drummer <a href="/wiki/Terry_Cox" title="Terry Cox">Terry Cox</a> was recruited to complete the recording of songs for the album. The leadoff single, "<a href="/wiki/Don%27t_Forget_to_Remember" title="Don't Forget to Remember">Don't Forget to Remember</a>" was a big hit in the UK reaching No. 2, but a disappointment in the US, only reaching No. 73. The next two singles, "<a href="/wiki/I.O.I.O." title="I.O.I.O.">I.O.I.O.</a>" and "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/If_I_Only_Had_My_Mind_on_Something_Else" title="If I Only Had My Mind on Something Else">If I Only Had My Mind on Something Else</a>" barely scraped the charts. On 1 December 1969, Barry and Maurice parted ways professionally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> After the album was released in early-1970, it seemed that the Bee Gees were finished. Maurice started to record his first solo album <i><a href="/wiki/The_Loner_(album)" title="The Loner (album)">The Loner</a></i> which was not released. Meanwhile, he released the single "<a href="/wiki/Railroad_(song)" title="Railroad (song)">Railroad</a>", and starred in the West End musical <i>Sing a Rude Song</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> In February 1970 Barry recorded a solo album which never saw official release either, though "<a href="/wiki/I%27ll_Kiss_Your_Memory" title="I'll Kiss Your Memory">I'll Kiss Your Memory</a>" was released as a single backed by "This Time" without much interest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1970.E2.80.9373">1970–73</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bee_Gees&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 1970–73">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bee_Gees_Midnight_Special_1973.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1083" data-file-width="846" height="282" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Bee_Gees_Midnight_Special_1973.jpg/220px-Bee_Gees_Midnight_Special_1973.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Bee_Gees_Midnight_Special_1973.jpg/330px-Bee_Gees_Midnight_Special_1973.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Bee_Gees_Midnight_Special_1973.jpg/440px-Bee_Gees_Midnight_Special_1973.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bee_Gees_Midnight_Special_1973.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Bee Gees performing at <i>The Midnight Special</i> in 1973.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the summer of 1970, according to Barry "Robin rang me in <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> where I was on holiday [saying] 'let's do it again'". By 21 August 1970, after they had got back together again, Barry announced that the Bee Gees "are there and they will never, ever part again". Maurice said "We just discussed it and re-formed. We want to apologize publicly to Robin for the things that have been said."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-were_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-were-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> Earlier in June 1970, Robin and Maurice recorded a dozen songs before Barry joined and included two songs that were on their reunion album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> Around the same time, Barry and Robin were about to publish the book <i>On the Other Hand</i>, which they started in Australia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-were_10-2"><a href="#cite_note-were-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> They also recruited Geoff Bridgford as the group's official drummer; Bridgford previously worked with <a href="/wiki/The_Groove_(band)" title="The Groove (band)">the Groove</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tin_Tin_(band)" title="Tin Tin (band)">Tin Tin</a> and played drums on Maurice's unreleased first solo album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/2_Years_On" title="2 Years On">2 Years On</a></i> was released in October in the US and November in the UK in 1970. The lead single "<a href="/wiki/Lonely_Days" title="Lonely Days">Lonely Days</a>" reached at No. 3 on the United States. Around the same time, the band appeared on <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Johnny_Cash_Show" title="The Johnny Cash Show">The Johnny Cash Show</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Carson" title="Johnny Carson">Johnny Carson</a>'s <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tonight_Show" title="Tonight Show">Tonight Show</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Andy_Williams_Show" title="The Andy Williams Show">The Andy Williams Show</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dick_Cavett_Show" title="The Dick Cavett Show">The Dick Cavett Show</a></i> and <i>The Ed Sullivan Show</i> to perform "Lonely Days".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-were_10-3"><a href="#cite_note-were-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> Their ninth album, <i><a href="/wiki/Trafalgar_(album)" title="Trafalgar (album)">Trafalgar</a></i>, was released in late 1971 that contains their first US No. 1 with "<a href="/wiki/How_Can_You_Mend_a_Broken_Heart" title="How Can You Mend a Broken Heart">How Can You Mend a Broken Heart</a>" while "<a href="/wiki/Israel_(Bee_Gees_song)" title="Israel (Bee Gees song)">Israel</a>" reached No. 22 in the Netherlands. "How Can You Mend a Broken Heart" also brought Bee Gees their first <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a> nomination for <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Pop_Performance_by_a_Duo_or_Group_with_Vocals" title="Grammy Award for Best Pop Performance by a Duo or Group with Vocals">Best Pop Performance by a Duo or Group with Vocals</a>. The group's songs were included in the soundtrack for the 1971 film <i><a href="/wiki/Melody_(1971_film)" title="Melody (1971 film)">Melody</a></i>. In 1972, they hit No. 16 in the US with the non-album single "<a href="/wiki/My_World_(Bee_Gees_song)" title="My World (Bee Gees song)">My World</a>" backed by Maurice's composition "<a href="/wiki/On_Time_(song)" title="On Time (song)">On Time</a>". Another 1972 single, "<a href="/wiki/Run_to_Me_(Bee_Gees_song)" title="Run to Me (Bee Gees song)">Run To Me</a>" from the LP <i><a href="/wiki/To_Whom_It_May_Concern_(Bee_Gees_album)" title="To Whom It May Concern (Bee Gees album)">To Whom It May Concern</a></i> returned them to the UK top ten for the first time in three years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Charts_24-4"><a href="#cite_note-Charts-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> In 24 November 1972, the band headlined the Woodstock of the West Festival at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Coliseum" title="Los Angeles Coliseum">Los Angeles Coliseum</a> (which was an answer to <a href="/wiki/Woodstock" title="Woodstock">Woodstock</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_York" title="New York">New York</a>, Eastern United States), the other performers are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sly_%26_The_Family_Stone" title="Sly &amp; The Family Stone">Sly &amp; The Family Stone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stevie_Wonder" title="Stevie Wonder">Stevie Wonder</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eagles_(band)" title="Eagles (band)">Eagles</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> Also in 1972, the group sang "<a href="/wiki/Hey_Jude" title="Hey Jude">Hey Jude</a>" with <a href="/wiki/Wilson_Pickett" title="Wilson Pickett">Wilson Pickett</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>By 1973, however, the Bee Gees were in a rut. The album, <i><a href="/wiki/Life_in_a_Tin_Can" title="Life in a Tin Can">Life in a Tin Can</a></i>, released on the newly formed <a href="/wiki/RSO_Records" title="RSO Records">RSO Records</a> and its lead-off single, "<a href="/wiki/Saw_a_New_Morning" title="Saw a New Morning">Saw a New Morning</a>", sold poorly with the single peaking at No. 94. This was followed by an unreleased album (known as <i><a href="/wiki/A_Kick_in_the_Head_Is_Worth_Eight_in_the_Pants" title="A Kick in the Head Is Worth Eight in the Pants">A Kick in the Head Is Worth Eight in the Pants</a></i>). A second compilation album, <i><a href="/wiki/Best_of_Bee_Gees,_Volume_2" title="Best of Bee Gees, Volume 2">Best of Bee Gees, Volume 2</a></i> was released in 1973 though it did not repeat the success of <a href="/wiki/Best_of_Bee_Gees" title="Best of Bee Gees">Volume 1</a>. On 6 April 1973 episode of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Midnight_Special_(TV_series)" title="The Midnight Special (TV series)">The Midnight Special</a></i> they performed "<a href="/wiki/Money_(That%27s_What_I_Want)" title="Money (That's What I Want)">Money (That's What I Want)</a>" with <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Lee_Lewis" title="Jerry Lee Lewis">Jerry Lee Lewis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> Also in 1973, they were invited by <a href="/wiki/Chuck_Berry" title="Chuck Berry">Chuck Berry</a> to perform with him onstage at <i>The Midnight Special</i> performing "<a href="/wiki/Johnny_B._Goode" title="Johnny B. Goode">Johnny B. Goode</a>"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> as well as "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reelin%27_and_Rockin" title="Reelin' and Rockin">Reelin' and Rockin</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>After a tour of United States in early 1974, the group ended up playing small clubs in England,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> most notably on Batley's Variety in <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a> and Barry said: "We ended up in, have you ever heard of Batley's the variety club in England?".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On the advice of <a href="/wiki/Ahmet_Erteg%C3%BCn" title="Ahmet Ertegün">Ahmet Ertegün</a>, head of their US label <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Records" title="Atlantic Records">Atlantic Records</a>, Stigwood arranged for the group to record with famed <a href="/wiki/Soul_music" title="Soul music">soul</a> music producer <a href="/wiki/Arif_Mardin" title="Arif Mardin">Arif Mardin</a>. The resulting LP, <i><a href="/wiki/Mr._Natural_(Bee_Gees_album)" title="Mr. Natural (Bee Gees album)">Mr. Natural</a></i>, included fewer ballads and foreshadowed the <a href="/wiki/Rhythm_and_blues" title="Rhythm and blues">R&amp;B</a> direction of the rest of their career. But when it too failed to attract much interest, Mardin encouraged them to work within the soul music style. The brothers attempted to assemble a live stage band that could replicate their studio sound. Lead guitarist <a href="/wiki/Alan_Kendall" title="Alan Kendall">Alan Kendall</a> had come on board in 1971, but did not have much to do until <i>Mr. Natural</i>. For that album, they added drummer Dennis Bryon, and they later added ex-<a href="/wiki/Strawbs" title="Strawbs">Strawbs</a> keyboard player Blue Weaver, completing the late 1970s Bee Gees band. Maurice, who had previously performed on piano, guitar, organ, <a href="/wiki/Mellotron" title="Mellotron">mellotron</a>, and bass guitar, as well as <a href="/wiki/Mandolin" title="Mandolin">mandolin</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moog_synthesiser" title="Moog synthesiser">Moog synthesiser</a>, now confined himself to bass onstage. In 1974, on the <i>Mr. Natural</i> tour, the Bee Gees played the Philippines at the <a href="/wiki/Cultural_Center_of_the_Philippines" title="Cultural Center of the Philippines">Cultural Center of the Philippines</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1975.E2.80.9379:_Turning_to_disco">1975–79: Turning to disco</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bee_Gees&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 1975–79: Turning to disco">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Main_Course_and_Children_of_the_World"><i>Main Course</i> and <i>Children of the World</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bee_Gees&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Main Course and Children of the World">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bee_Gees%27_wordmark_logo_(1975-1981).gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="100" data-file-width="398" height="55" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/92/Bee_Gees%27_wordmark_logo_%281975-1981%29.gif/220px-Bee_Gees%27_wordmark_logo_%281975-1981%29.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/92/Bee_Gees%27_wordmark_logo_%281975-1981%29.gif/330px-Bee_Gees%27_wordmark_logo_%281975-1981%29.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/9/92/Bee_Gees%27_wordmark_logo_%281975-1981%29.gif 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bee_Gees%27_wordmark_logo_(1975-1981).gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bee Gees' wordmark logo (1975–1981)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At <a href="/wiki/Eric_Clapton" title="Eric Clapton">Eric Clapton</a>'s suggestion, the brothers relocated to Miami, Florida, early in 1975 to record music. After starting off with ballads, they eventually heeded the urging of Mardin and Stigwood and crafted more rhythmic <a href="/wiki/Disco" title="Disco">disco</a> songs, including their second US No. 1, "<a href="/wiki/Jive_Talkin%27" title="Jive Talkin'">Jive Talkin'</a>", along with US No. 7 "<a href="/wiki/Nights_on_Broadway" title="Nights on Broadway">Nights on Broadway</a>". The band liked the resulting new sound. This time the public agreed by sending the LP <i><a href="/wiki/Main_Course" title="Main Course">Main Course</a></i> up the charts. This album included the first Bee Gees songs where Barry used falsetto,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> something that would later become a trademark of the Bee Gees. This was also the first Bee Gees album to have two US top-10 singles since 1968's <i>Idea</i>. <i>Main Course</i> also became their first charting R&amp;B album. Mardin was unable to work with the group afterwards, but the Bee Gees enlisted <a href="/wiki/Albhy_Galuten" title="Albhy Galuten">Albhy Galuten</a> and Karl Richardson, who had worked with Mardin during the <i>Main Course</i> sessions. This production team would carry the Bee Gees through the rest of the 1970s. On the Bee Gees' appearance on <i>The Midnight Special</i> in 1975 to promote <i>Main Course</i>, they sing "To Love Somebody" with <a href="/wiki/Helen_Reddy" title="Helen Reddy">Helen Reddy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Around the same time, the Bee Gees had recorded three Beatles covers—"<a href="/wiki/Golden_Slumbers" title="Golden Slumbers">Golden Slumbers</a>/<a href="/wiki/Carry_That_Weight" title="Carry That Weight">Carry That Weight</a>", "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/She_Came_in_Through_the_Bathroom_Window" title="She Came in Through the Bathroom Window">She Came in Through the Bathroom Window</a>" with Barry providing lead vocals and "<a href="/wiki/Sun_King_(song)" title="Sun King (song)">Sun King</a>" with Maurice providing lead vocals, for the transitory musical documentary <i><a href="/wiki/All_This_and_World_War_II" title="All This and World War II">All This and World War II</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The next album, <i><a href="/wiki/Children_of_the_World" title="Children of the World">Children of the World</a></i> released in September 1976 was drenched in Barry's new-found falsetto and Weaver's <a href="/wiki/Synthesizer" title="Synthesizer">synthesizer</a> disco licks. Led off by the single "<a href="/wiki/You_Should_Be_Dancing" title="You Should Be Dancing">You Should Be Dancing</a>" which features <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Percussion" title="Percussion">percussion</a> work by musician <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Stills" title="Stephen Stills">Stephen Stills</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> The song pushed the Bee Gees to a level of stardom they had not previously achieved in the US, though their new R&amp;B/disco sound was not as popular with some die hard fans from the 1960s. Another single from the album the pop ballad "<a href="/wiki/Love_So_Right" title="Love So Right">Love So Right</a>" reached No. 3 in the US and "<a href="/wiki/Boogie_Child" title="Boogie Child">Boogie Child</a>" (US No. 12) in January 1977.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> The album peaked at No. 8 in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> A compilation <i><a href="/wiki/Bee_Gees_Gold" title="Bee Gees Gold">Bee Gees Gold</a></i> was released in November, it contains the group's hits from 1967-1971.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Saturday_Night_Fever_and_Spirits_Having_Flown"><i>Saturday Night Fever</i> and <i>Spirits Having Flown</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bee_Gees&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Saturday Night Fever and Spirits Having Flown">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Following a successful live album, <i><a href="/wiki/Here_at_Last..._Bee_Gees..._Live" title="Here at Last... Bee Gees... Live">Here at Last... Bee Gees... Live</a></i>, the Bee Gees agreed with Stigwood to participate in the creation of the <i><a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Fever_(soundtrack)" title="Saturday Night Fever (soundtrack)">Saturday Night Fever soundtrack</a></i>. It would be the turning point of their career. The cultural impact of both the film and the soundtrack was seismic throughout the world, prolonging the <a href="/wiki/Disco" title="Disco">disco</a> scene's mainstream appeal.</p>
<p>The band's involvement in the film did not begin until post-production. As <a href="/wiki/John_Travolta" title="John Travolta">John Travolta</a> asserted, "The Bee Gees weren't even involved in the movie in the beginning ... I was dancing to <a href="/wiki/Stevie_Wonder" title="Stevie Wonder">Stevie Wonder</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boz_Scaggs" title="Boz Scaggs">Boz Scaggs</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kashner_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kashner-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> Producer Robert Stigwood commissioned the Bee Gees to create the songs for the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> The brothers wrote the songs "virtually in a single weekend" at <a href="/wiki/Ch%C3%A2teau_d%27H%C3%A9rouville" title="Château d'Hérouville">Château d'Hérouville studio</a> in France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kashner_49-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kashner-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> Barry Gibb remembered the reaction when Stigwood and music supervisor Bill Oakes arrived and listened to the demos:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>They flipped out and said these will be great. We still had no concept of the movie, except some kind of rough script that they'd brought with them... You've got to remember, we were fairly dead in the water at that point, 1975, somewhere in that zone—the Bee Gees' sound was basically tired. We needed something new. We hadn't had a hit record in about three years. So we felt, Oh Jeez, that's it. That's our life span, like most groups in the late 60s. So, we had to find something. We didn't know what was going to happen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kashner_49-2"><a href="#cite_note-Kashner-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>Bill Oakes, who supervised the soundtrack, asserts that <i><a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Fever" title="Saturday Night Fever">Saturday Night Fever</a></i> did not begin the disco craze; rather, it prolonged it: "Disco had run its course. These days, <i>Fever</i> is credited with kicking off the whole disco thing—it really didn't. Truth is, it breathed new life into a genre that was actually dying."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kashner_49-3"><a href="#cite_note-Kashner-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Three Bee Gees singles "<a href="/wiki/How_Deep_Is_Your_Love" title="How Deep Is Your Love">How Deep Is Your Love</a>" (US No. 1, UK No. 3), "<a href="/wiki/Stayin%27_Alive" title="Stayin' Alive">Stayin' Alive</a>" (US No. 1, UK No. 4) and "<a href="/wiki/Night_Fever" title="Night Fever">Night Fever</a>" (US No. 1, UK No. 1) charted high in many countries around the world, launching the most popular period of the disco era.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Charts_24-5"><a href="#cite_note-Charts-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> They also penned the song "<a href="/wiki/If_I_Can%27t_Have_You" title="If I Can't Have You">If I Can't Have You</a>" which became a US No. 1 hit for <a href="/wiki/Yvonne_Elliman" title="Yvonne Elliman">Yvonne Elliman</a>, while the Bee Gees' own version was the B-Side of "Stayin' Alive". Such was the popularity of <i>Saturday Night Fever</i> that two different versions of the song "<a href="/wiki/More_Than_a_Woman_(Bee_Gees_song)" title="More Than a Woman (Bee Gees song)">More Than a Woman</a>" received airplay, one by the Bee Gees, which was relegated to album track, and another by <a href="/wiki/Tavares_(group)" title="Tavares (group)">Tavares</a>, which was the hit. The Gibb sound was inescapable. During an eight-month period beginning in the Christmas season of 1977, six songs written by the brothers held the No. 1 position on the US charts for 25 of 32 consecutive weeks—three of their own releases, two for brother <a href="/wiki/Andy_Gibb" title="Andy Gibb">Andy Gibb</a>, and the Yvonne Elliman single.</p>
<p>Fuelled by the movie's success, the soundtrack broke multiple industry records, becoming the highest-selling album in recording history to that point. With more than 40 million copies sold, <i>Saturday Night Fever</i> is among music's top five best selling soundtrack albums. As of 2010, it is calculated as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_albums_worldwide" title="List of best-selling albums worldwide">4th highest-selling album</a> worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Everyhit_records_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-Everyhit_records-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> For <i>Saturday Night Fever</i> the Bee Gees won five <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Awards</a>: <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Album_of_the_Year" title="Grammy Award for Album of the Year">Album of the Year</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Producer_of_the_Year,_Non-Classical" title="Grammy Award for Producer of the Year, Non-Classical">Producer of the Year</a> (with Albhy Galuten and Karl Richardson), two awards for <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Pop_Performance_by_a_Duo_or_Group_with_Vocals" title="Grammy Award for Best Pop Performance by a Duo or Group with Vocals">Best Pop Performance by a Duo or Group with Vocals</a> (one in 1978 for "How Deep Is Your Love" and one in 1979 for "Stayin' Alive") and <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Vocal_Arrangement_for_Two_or_More_Voices" title="Grammy Award for Best Vocal Arrangement for Two or More Voices">Best Vocal Arrangement for Two or More Voices</a> for "Stayin' Alive".</p>
<p>During this era, Barry and Robin also wrote "<a href="/wiki/Emotion_(Samantha_Sang_song)" title="Emotion (Samantha Sang song)">Emotion</a>" for an old friend, Australian vocalist <a href="/wiki/Samantha_Sang" title="Samantha Sang">Samantha Sang</a>, who made it a Top Ten hit (the Bee Gees sang backing vocals). Barry also wrote the title song to the movie version of the Broadway musical <i><a href="/wiki/Grease_(musical)" title="Grease (musical)">Grease</a></i> for <a href="/wiki/Frankie_Valli" title="Frankie Valli">Frankie Valli</a> to perform, which went to No. 1. During this period, the Bee Gees' younger brother <a href="/wiki/Andy_Gibb" title="Andy Gibb">Andy</a> followed his older siblings into a music career, and enjoyed considerable success. Produced by Barry, Andy Gibb's first three singles all topped the US charts. In March 1978, the Bee Gees held the top 2 positions on the US Charts with "Night Fever" and "Stayin' Alive", the first time this had happened since the Beatles. On the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> chart for 25 March 1978, five songs written by the Gibbs were in the US top ten at the same time: "Night Fever", "Stayin' Alive", "If I Can't Have You", "Emotion" and "Love is Thicker Than Water". Such chart dominance had not been seen since April 1964, when the Beatles had all five of the top five American singles. Barry Gibb became the only songwriter to have four consecutive number one hits in the US, breaking the John Lennon and Paul McCartney 1964 record. These songs were "Stayin' Alive", "Love Is Thicker Than Water", "Night Fever", and "If I Can't Have You".</p>
<p>The Bee Gees also co-starred with <a href="/wiki/Peter_Frampton" title="Peter Frampton">Peter Frampton</a> in the movie <i><a href="/wiki/Sgt._Pepper%27s_Lonely_Hearts_Club_Band_(film)" title="Sgt. Pepper's Lonely Hearts Club Band (film)">Sgt. Pepper's Lonely Hearts Club Band</a></i> (1978), loosely inspired by the classic 1967 album by The Beatles. The film had been heavily promoted prior to release, and was expected to enjoy great commercial success. However, the disjointed film was savaged by the movie critics, and ignored by the public. Though some of its tracks charted, the soundtrack too was a high-profile flop. The single "<a href="/wiki/Oh!_Darling" title="Oh! Darling">Oh! Darling</a>", credited to Robin Gibb, reached No. 15 in the US.</p>
<p>The Bee Gees' follow-up to <i>Saturday Night Fever</i> was the <i><a href="/wiki/Spirits_Having_Flown" title="Spirits Having Flown">Spirits Having Flown</a></i> album. It yielded three more hits: "<a href="/wiki/Too_Much_Heaven" title="Too Much Heaven">Too Much Heaven</a>" (US No. 1, UK No. 3), "<a href="/wiki/Tragedy_(Bee_Gees_song)" title="Tragedy (Bee Gees song)">Tragedy</a>" (US No. 1, UK No. 1) and "<a href="/wiki/Love_You_Inside_Out" title="Love You Inside Out">Love You Inside Out</a>" (US No. 1).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Charts_24-6"><a href="#cite_note-Charts-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> This gave the act six consecutive No. 1 singles in the US within a year and a half (a record surpassed only by <a href="/wiki/Whitney_Houston" title="Whitney Houston">Whitney Houston</a>). "Too Much Heaven" ended up as the Bee Gees' musical contribution to the <a href="/wiki/Music_for_UNICEF_Concert" title="Music for UNICEF Concert">Music for UNICEF Concert</a> at the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">United Nations General Assembly</a> in January 1979, a benefit organised by the Bee Gees, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Stigwood" title="Robert Stigwood">Robert Stigwood</a>, and <a href="/wiki/David_Frost" title="David Frost">David Frost</a> for <a href="/wiki/UNICEF" title="UNICEF">UNICEF</a> that was broadcast worldwide. The brothers donated the royalties from the song to the charity. Up to 2007, this song has earned over $11 million for <a href="/wiki/UNICEF" title="UNICEF">UNICEF</a>. During the summer of 1979, the Bee Gees embarked on their largest concert tour covering the US and Canada. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1979_Spirits_Having_Flown_Tour" title="1979 Spirits Having Flown Tour">Spirits Having Flown tour</a> capitalised on Bee Gees fever that was sweeping the nation, with sold out concerts in 38 cities. The Bee Gees produced a video for the title track of "<a href="/wiki/Too_Much_Heaven" title="Too Much Heaven">Too Much Heaven</a>", directed by Miami-based filmmaker Martin Pitts and produced by Charles Allen. With this video, Pitts and Allen began a long association with the brothers.</p>
<p>The Bee Gees even had a country hit in 1979 with "<a href="/wiki/Rest_Your_Love_on_Me" title="Rest Your Love on Me">Rest Your Love on Me</a>", the flip side of their pop hit "Too Much Heaven", which made Top 40 on the country charts. In 1981, <a href="/wiki/Conway_Twitty" title="Conway Twitty">Conway Twitty</a>'s version of "Rest Your Love on Me" topped the <a href="/wiki/Country_music" title="Country music">country</a> charts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The Bee Gees' overwhelming success rose and fell with the disco bubble. By the end of 1979, disco was rapidly declining in popularity, and the backlash against disco put the Bee Gees' American career in a tailspin. Radio stations around the US began promoting "Bee Gee Free Weekends". Following their remarkable run from 1975 to 1979, the act would have only one more top ten single in the US, and that would not come until 1989. The Bee Gees' international popularity sustained somewhat less damage. Barry Gibb considered the success of the <i>Saturday Night Fever</i> soundtrack both a blessing and a curse:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p><i>Fever</i> was No. 1 every week... It wasn't just like a hit album. It was No. 1 every single week for 25 weeks. It was just an amazing, crazy, extraordinary time. I remember not being able to answer the phone, and I remember people climbing over my walls. I was quite grateful when it stopped. It was too unreal. In the long run, your life is better if it's not like that on a constant basis. Nice though it was.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kashner_49-4"><a href="#cite_note-Kashner-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1980.E2.80.9386:_Outside_projects.2C_band_turmoil.2C_solo_efforts_and_decline">1980–86: Outside projects, band turmoil, solo efforts and decline</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bee_Gees&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 1980–86: Outside projects, band turmoil, solo efforts and decline">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Robin co-produced <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Ruffin" title="Jimmy Ruffin">Jimmy Ruffin</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Sunrise_(Jimmy_Ruffin_album)" title="Sunrise (Jimmy Ruffin album)">Sunrise</a></i> released in May 1980 but the songs were started in 1979; the album contains songs which were written by the Gibb brothers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> In March 1980, Barry Gibb worked with <a href="/wiki/Barbra_Streisand" title="Barbra Streisand">Barbra Streisand</a> on her album <i><a href="/wiki/Guilty_(Barbra_Streisand_album)" title="Guilty (Barbra Streisand album)">Guilty</a></i>. He co-produced and wrote or co-wrote all nine of the album's tracks (four of them written with Robin and the title track with both Robin and Maurice). Barry also appeared on the album's cover with Streisand, and duetted with her on two tracks. The album reached No. 1 in both the US and the UK, as did the single "<a href="/wiki/Woman_in_Love" title="Woman in Love">Woman in Love</a>" (written by Barry and Robin), becoming Streisand's most successful single and album to date. Both of the Streisand/Gibb duets, "<a href="/wiki/Guilty_(Barbra_Streisand_and_Barry_Gibb_song)" title="Guilty (Barbra Streisand and Barry Gibb song)">Guilty</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/What_Kind_of_Fool" title="What Kind of Fool">What Kind of Fool</a>", also reached the US top 10. In October, the Bee Gees regrouped to record songs that would go onto their upcoming album but wasn't continued and Weaver, Kendall (returned in 1987) and Bryon left the group and the brothers later recruited some studio musicians.</p>
<p>In 1981, the Bee Gees released the album <i><a href="/wiki/Living_Eyes_(Bee_Gees_album)" title="Living Eyes (Bee Gees album)">Living Eyes</a></i>, their last full-length album release on RSO. This album was the first CD ever played in public, when it was played to viewers of the BBC show <i><a href="/wiki/Tomorrow%27s_World" title="Tomorrow's World">Tomorrow's World</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> With the disco backlash still running strong, the album failed to make the UK or US Top 40—breaking their streak of Top 40 hits, which started in 1975 with "<a href="/wiki/Jive_Talkin%27" title="Jive Talkin'">Jive Talkin'</a>". Two singles from the album fared little better—"<a href="/wiki/He%27s_a_Liar" title="He's a Liar">He's a Liar</a>", reaching No. 30 in the US and "<a href="/wiki/Living_Eyes_(song)" title="Living Eyes (song)">Living Eyes</a>", reaching No. 45.</p>
<p>In 1982, <a href="/wiki/Dionne_Warwick" title="Dionne Warwick">Dionne Warwick</a> enjoyed a UK No. 2 and US <a href="/wiki/Adult_Contemporary_(chart)" title="Adult Contemporary (chart)">Adult Contemporary No. 1</a> hit with her comeback single, "<a href="/wiki/Heartbreaker_(Dionne_Warwick_song)" title="Heartbreaker (Dionne Warwick song)">Heartbreaker</a>", taken from her <a href="/wiki/Heartbreaker_(Dionne_Warwick_album)" title="Heartbreaker (Dionne Warwick album)">album of the same name</a> written largely by the Bee Gees and co-produced by Barry Gibb. The album reached No. 3 in the UK and the Top 30 in the US, where it was certified Gold. A year later <a href="/wiki/Dolly_Parton" title="Dolly Parton">Dolly Parton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kenny_Rogers" title="Kenny Rogers">Kenny Rogers</a> recorded the Bee Gees-penned track "<a href="/wiki/Islands_in_the_Stream_(song)" title="Islands in the Stream (song)">Islands in the Stream</a>", which became a US No. 1 hit and entered the Top 10 in the UK. Rogers' 1983 album, <i><a href="/wiki/Eyes_That_See_in_the_Dark" title="Eyes That See in the Dark">Eyes That See in the Dark</a></i>, was written entirely by the Bee Gees and co-produced by Barry. The album was a Top 10 hit in the US and was certified Double Platinum. The Bee Gees had greater success with the soundtrack to <i><a href="/wiki/Staying_Alive_(1983_film)" title="Staying Alive (1983 film)">Staying Alive</a></i> in 1983, the sequel to <i><a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Fever" title="Saturday Night Fever">Saturday Night Fever</a></i>. The soundtrack was certified platinum in the US, and included their Top 30 hit "<a href="/wiki/The_Woman_in_You" title="The Woman in You">The Woman in You</a>". Also in 1983, the band was sued by Chicago songwriter <a href="/wiki/Selle_v._Gibb" title="Selle v. Gibb">Ronald Selle</a>, who claimed that the brothers stole melodic material from one of his songs, "Let It End", and used it in "How Deep Is Your Love". At first, the Bee Gees lost the case; one juror said that a factor in the jury's decision was the Gibbs' failure to introduce expert testimony rebutting the plaintiff's expert testimony that it was "impossible" for the two songs to have been written independently. However, the verdict was overturned a few months later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In August 1983, Barry had signed a solo deal with MCA Records and he spent much of late 1983 and 1984 writing songs for this first solo effort.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> While Robin, on the other hand, released two solo albums in the 80s, <i><a href="/wiki/How_Old_Are_You%3F_(album)" title="How Old Are You? (album)">How Old Are You?</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Secret_Agent_(Robin_Gibb_album)" title="Secret Agent (Robin Gibb album)">Secret Agent</a></i>. And Maurice released his second single up to date "<a href="/wiki/Hold_Her_in_Your_Hand" title="Hold Her in Your Hand">Hold Her in Your Hand</a>" for the first time since 1970.</p>
<p>In 1985, <a href="/wiki/Diana_Ross" title="Diana Ross">Diana Ross</a> released the album <i><a href="/wiki/Eaten_Alive_(album)" title="Eaten Alive (album)">Eaten Alive</a></i>, written by the Bee Gees, with the title track co-written with <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a> (who also performed on the track). The album was again co-produced by Barry Gibb and the single "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chain_Reaction_(song)" title="Chain Reaction (song)">Chain Reaction</a>" gave Ross a UK and Australian No. 1 hit.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1987.E2.80.9399:_Comeback_and_return_to_popularity">1987–99: Comeback and return to popularity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bee_Gees&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 1987–99: Comeback and return to popularity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Bee Gees released the album <i><a href="/wiki/E.S.P._(Bee_Gees_album)" title="E.S.P. (Bee Gees album)">E.S.P.</a></i> in 1987, which sold over 3 million copies. It was their first album in six years, and their first for <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros._Records" title="Warner Bros. Records">Warner Bros. Records</a>. The single "<a href="/wiki/You_Win_Again_(Bee_Gees_song)" title="You Win Again (Bee Gees song)">You Win Again</a>" went to No. 1 in numerous countries, including the UK,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UKCharts_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-UKCharts-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> and made the Bee Gees the first group to score a UK No. 1 hit in each of three decades: the 1960s, 1970s, and 1980s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> The single was a disappointment in the US, charting at No. 75, and the Bee Gees voiced their frustration over American radio stations not playing their new European hit single, an omission which the group felt led to poor sales of their current album in the States. On 10 March 1988, younger brother <a href="/wiki/Andy_Gibb" title="Andy Gibb">Andy</a> died, aged 30, as a result of <a href="/wiki/Myocarditis" title="Myocarditis">myocarditis</a>, an inflammation of the heart muscle due to a recent viral infection. His brothers acknowledge that Andy's past drug and alcohol use probably made his heart more susceptible to this illness. Just before Andy's death, the brothers had decided that Andy would join them, which would have made them a four-piece group. The Bee Gees' following album, <i><a href="/wiki/One_(Bee_Gees_album)" title="One (Bee Gees album)">One</a></i> (1989), featured a song dedicated to Andy, "Wish You Were Here". The album also contained their first US top ten hit (No. 7) in a decade, "One" (an Adult Contemporary No. 1). After the album's release, the band embarked on its first world tour in ten years.</p>
<p>In 1990, <a href="/wiki/Polydor_Records" title="Polydor Records">Polydor Records</a> issued the box set <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tales_from_the_Brothers_Gibb:_A_History_in_Song" title="Tales from the Brothers Gibb: A History in Song">Tales from the Brothers Gibb: A History in Song</a></i>, which contains all singles released (except 1981's "Living Eyes"), rare B-sides, unreleased tracks, solo material, and live performances. Many songs received new stereo mixes by <a href="/wiki/Bill_Inglot" title="Bill Inglot">Bill Inglot</a> with some songs making their CD debut. At the time of its release, <i>Tales</i> was one of the first box sets issued in the music business and it was considered an honour for a group to have one. In the UK, Polydor issued a single disc hits collection from <i>Tales</i> called <i><a href="/wiki/The_Very_Best_of_the_Bee_Gees" title="The Very Best of the Bee Gees">The Very Best of the Bee Gees</a></i>, which contained their biggest UK hits. The album became one of their best selling albums in that country, eventually being certified Triple Platinum.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bee_Gees_1992.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="566" data-file-width="756" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Bee_Gees_1992.JPG/220px-Bee_Gees_1992.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Bee_Gees_1992.JPG/330px-Bee_Gees_1992.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Bee_Gees_1992.JPG/440px-Bee_Gees_1992.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bee_Gees_1992.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bee Gees in Los Angeles in 1992</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Following their next album, <i><a href="/wiki/High_Civilization" title="High Civilization">High Civilization</a></i> (1991), which contained the UK top five hit "<a href="/wiki/Secret_Love_(Bee_Gees_song)" title="Secret Love (Bee Gees song)">Secret Love</a>", the Bee Gees went on a European tour. After the tour, Barry Gibb began to battle a serious back problem, which required surgery. In addition, he also suffered from <a href="/wiki/Arthritis" title="Arthritis">arthritis</a>, and at one point, it was so severe that it was doubtful that he would be able to play guitar for much longer. Also in the early 1990s, Maurice Gibb finally sought treatment for his alcoholism, which he had battled for many years, with the help of <a href="/wiki/Alcoholics_Anonymous" title="Alcoholics Anonymous">Alcoholics Anonymous</a>.</p>
