<p>In 1993, the group returned to the Polydor label, and released the album <i><a href="/wiki/Size_Isn%27t_Everything" title="Size Isn't Everything">Size Isn't Everything</a></i>, which contained the UK top five hit "For Whom the Bell Tolls". Success still eluded them in the US, however, as the first single released, "<a href="/wiki/Paying_the_Price_of_Love" title="Paying the Price of Love">Paying the Price of Love</a>" only managed to reach No. 74 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> while the parent album stalled at No. 153.</p>
<p>In 1997, they released the album <i><a href="/wiki/Still_Waters_(Bee_Gees_album)" title="Still Waters (Bee Gees album)">Still Waters</a></i>, which sold over four million copies, and reached No.2 in the UK (their highest album chart position there since 1979) and No.11 in the US. The album's first single, "<a href="/wiki/Alone_(Bee_Gees_song)" title="Alone (Bee Gees song)">Alone</a>", gave them another UK Top 5 hit and a top 30 hit in the US. <i>Still Waters</i> would be the band's most successful US release of their post-RSO era.</p>
<p>At the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1997_BRIT_Awards" title="1997 BRIT Awards">1997 BRIT Awards</a> held in <a href="/wiki/Earls_Court_Exhibition_Centre" title="Earls Court Exhibition Centre">Earls Court</a>, London on 24 February, the Bee Gees received the award for Outstanding Contribution to Music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1997Awards_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-1997Awards-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> On 14 November 1997, the Bee Gees performed a live concert in <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Valley" title="Las Vegas Valley">Las Vegas</a> called <i><a href="/wiki/One_Night_Only_(Bee_Gees_album)" title="One Night Only (Bee Gees album)">One Night Only</a></i>. The show included a performance of "Our Love (Don't Throw It All Away)" synchronised with a vocal by their deceased brother Andy and a cameo appearance by <a href="/wiki/Celine_Dion" title="Celine Dion">Celine Dion</a> singing "<a href="/wiki/Immortality_(Celine_Dion_song)" title="Immortality (Celine Dion song)">Immortality</a>". The CD of the performance sold over 5 million copies. The "One Night Only" name grew out of the band's declaration that, due to Barry's health issues, the Las Vegas show was to be the final live performance of their career. After the immensely positive audience response to the Vegas concert, Barry decided to continue despite the pain, and the concert expanded into their last full-blown world tour of "One Night Only" concerts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBilyeuCookHughes2009_23-5"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBilyeuCookHughes2009-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (December 2013)">page needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The tour included playing to 56,000 people at London's <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium_(1923)" title="Wembley Stadium (1923)">Wembley Stadium</a> on 5 September 1998 and concluded in the newly built <a href="/wiki/Stadium_Australia" title="Stadium Australia">Olympic Stadium</a> in Sydney, Australia on 27 March 1999 to 72,000 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBilyeuCookHughes2009_23-6"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBilyeuCookHughes2009-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (December 2013)">page needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In 1998, the group's soundtrack for <i>Saturday Night Fever</i> was incorporated into a <a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Fever_(musical)" title="Saturday Night Fever (musical)">stage production</a> produced first in the West End and then on Broadway. They wrote three new songs for the adaptation. Also in 1998 the brothers recorded <i><a href="/wiki/Ellan_Vannin_(poem)" title="Ellan Vannin (poem)">Ellan Vannin</a></i> for <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man" title="Isle of Man">Isle of Man</a> charities. Known as the unofficial national anthem of the Isle of Man, the brothers performed the song during their world tour to reflect their pride in the place of their birth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The Bee Gees closed the decade with what turned out to be their last full-sized concert, known as <i>BG2K</i>, on 31 December 1999.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2000.E2.80.9308:_This_Is_Where_I_Came_In_and_Maurice.27s_death">2000–08: <i>This Is Where I Came In</i> and Maurice's death</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bee_Gees&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: 2000–08: This Is Where I Came In and Maurice's death">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2001, the group released what turned out to be their final album of new material as a group, <i><a href="/wiki/This_Is_Where_I_Came_In" title="This Is Where I Came In">This Is Where I Came In</a></i>. The album was another success, reaching the Top 10 in the UK (being certified Gold), and the Top 20 in the US. The title track was also a UK Top 20 hit single. The album gave each member of the group a chance to write in his own way, as well as composing songs together. For example, Maurice's compositions and leads are the "Man in the Middle" and "Walking on Air", while Robin contributed "Déjà Vu", "Promise the Earth", and "Embrace", and Barry contributed "Loose Talk Costs Lives", "Technicolour Dreams", and "Voice in the Wilderness". The other songs are collaborative in writing and vocals. They performed many tracks from <i>This Is Where I Came In</i>, plus many of their biggest hits, on the live televised concert series <i><a href="/wiki/Live_by_Request" title="Live by Request">Live by Request</a></i>, shown on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A%26E_Network" title="A&amp;E Network">A&amp;E Network</a>. The last concert of the Bee Gees as a trio was at the <i>Love and Hope Ball</i> in 2002.</p>
<p>Maurice, who had been the musical director of the Bee Gees during their final years as a group, died suddenly on 12 January 2003 at the age of 53 from a heart attack, while awaiting emergency surgery to repair a <a href="/wiki/Bowel_infarction" title="Bowel infarction">strangulated intestine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> Initially, his surviving brothers announced that they intended to carry on the name "Bee Gees" in his memory. But as time passed they decided to retire the group name, leaving it to represent the three brothers together.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The same week that Maurice died, Robin's solo album <i><a href="/wiki/Magnet_(album)" title="Magnet (album)">Magnet</a></i> was released. On 23 February 2003, the Bee Gees received the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Legend_Award" title="Grammy Legend Award">Grammy Legend Award</a>, they also became the first recipients of that award in the 21st century. Barry and Robin accepted as well as Maurice's son, Adam, in a tearful ceremony.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Although there was talk of a memorial concert featuring both surviving brothers and invited guests,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> nothing materialised. Barry and Robin continued to work independently, and both released recordings with other artists, occasionally coming together to perform at special events.</p>
<p>In late 2004, Robin embarked on a solo tour of Germany, Russia and Asia. During January 2005, Barry, Robin and several legendary <a href="/wiki/One_World_Project" title="One World Project">rock artists</a> recorded "Grief Never Grows Old", the official <a href="/wiki/Humanitarian_response_to_the_2004_Indian_Ocean_earthquake#Fundraising_events" title="Humanitarian response to the 2004 Indian Ocean earthquake">tsunami relief</a> record for the <a href="/wiki/Disasters_Emergency_Committee" title="Disasters Emergency Committee">Disasters Emergency Committee</a>. Later that year, Barry reunited with <a href="/wiki/Barbra_Streisand" title="Barbra Streisand">Barbra Streisand</a> for her top-selling album <i><a href="/wiki/Guilty_Pleasures_(Barbra_Streisand_album)" title="Guilty Pleasures (Barbra Streisand album)">Guilty Pleasures</a></i>, released as <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guilty_Too" title="Guilty Too">Guilty Too</a></i> in the UK as a sequel album to the previous <i><a href="/wiki/Guilty_(Barbra_Streisand_album)" title="Guilty (Barbra Streisand album)">Guilty</a></i>. Robin continued touring in Europe. Also in 2004, Barry recorded his song "I Cannot Give You My Love" with <a href="/wiki/Cliff_Richard" title="Cliff Richard">Cliff Richard</a>, which became a UK top 20 hit single.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In February 2006, Barry and Robin reunited on stage for a Miami charity concert to benefit the Diabetes Research Institute. It was their first public performance together since the death of brother Maurice. Barry and Robin also played at the 30th annual <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prince%27s_Trust" title="Prince's Trust">Prince's Trust</a> Concert in the UK on 20 May 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> In October 2008, Robin performed a couple of songs in London as part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BBC_Electric_Proms#25_October" title="BBC Electric Proms">BBC Electric Proms</a> <i>Saturday Night Fever</i> performance. This involved various other performers and the BBC Concert Orchestra and was screened on the BBC and BBC interactive services.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2009.E2.80.9312:_Return_to_performing_and_Robin.27s_death">2009–12: Return to performing and Robin's death</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bee_Gees&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: 2009–12: Return to performing and Robin's death">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In an interview with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Easy_Mix" title="Easy Mix">Easy Mix</a> radio host Tim Roxborough on 1 September 2009, Barry's 63rd birthday, Barry commented on future tours saying that "they will be back"; but in an agreement with Warner/Rhino they would not make an announcement at that time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> On 7 September 2009, Robin disclosed to <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Agnew" title="Jonathan Agnew">Jonathan Agnew</a> that he had been in touch with Barry and that they had agreed that the Bee Gees would re-form and "perform again".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Barry and Robin performed on the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Strictly_Come_Dancing" title="Strictly Come Dancing">Strictly Come Dancing</a></i> on 31 October 2009<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> and appeared on <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">ABC-TV</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Dancing_with_the_Stars_(U.S._TV_series)" title="Dancing with the Stars (U.S. TV series)">Dancing with the Stars</a></i> on 17 November 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> On 15 March 2010, Barry and Robin inducted the Swedish group <a href="/wiki/ABBA" title="ABBA">ABBA</a> into the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> On 26 May 2010, the two made a surprise appearance on the ninth season finale of <i><a href="/wiki/American_Idol" title="American Idol">American Idol</a></i>.</p>
<p>In October 2010, Robin Gibb was interviewed by the <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Mail" title="Daily Mail">Daily Mail</a></i>, and confirmed that the story of the Bee Gees was to be made into a Hollywood movie by <a href="/wiki/Steven_Spielberg" title="Steven Spielberg">Steven Spielberg</a>. Robin told the <i>Daily Mail</i>: "The movie is going to be done by some very important people. It will be our life story. Barry and I will be involved in the technical side". One of the challenges for Spielberg will be replicating the brothers' distinctive three-part harmonies and Barry's falsetto voice. Robin said: "I'd like our original recordings to be used because it's very hard to emulate them."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 20 November 2011 it was announced that Robin Gibb, at 61 years old, was diagnosed with <a href="/wiki/Liver_cancer" title="Liver cancer">liver cancer</a>, a condition he became aware of several months earlier. He had become noticeably thinner in previous months and had to cancel several appearances due to issues with severe abdominal pain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 13 February 2012, Robin joined British military trio <a href="/wiki/The_Soldiers" title="The Soldiers">The Soldiers</a> for the Coming Home charity concert at the <a href="/wiki/London_Palladium" title="London Palladium">London Palladium</a>, in support of injured servicemen. It was his first public appearance for almost five months, and his final.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 14 April 2012, it was reported that Robin had contracted <a href="/wiki/Pneumonia" title="Pneumonia">pneumonia</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> in a <a href="/wiki/Chelsea,_London" title="Chelsea, London">Chelsea</a> hospital and was in a coma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> Although he came out of his coma on 20 April 2012, his condition deteriorated rapidly,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> and he died on 20 May 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> With Robin's death, Barry became the last surviving Gibb brother, and the Bee Gees became defunct.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2012.E2.80.93present:_After_the_break-up">2012–present: After the break-up</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bee_Gees&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: 2012–present: After the break-up">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In September and October 2013, Barry performed his <a href="/wiki/Mythology_Tour" title="Mythology Tour">first solo tour</a> "in honour of his brothers and a lifetime of music". In addition to the Rhino Collection, <i>The Studio Albums: 1967–1968</i>, Warner Bros. released a box set in 2014 called <i>The Warner Bros Years: 1987-1991</i> that included the studio albums <i>E.S.P.</i>, <i>One</i>, and <i>High Civilization</i> as well as extended mixes and B-sides. It also included the band's entire 1989 concert in <a href="/wiki/Melbourne" title="Melbourne">Melbourne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, available only on video as "All For One" prior to this release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> The documentary <i>The Joy of the Bee Gees</i> is aired on <a href="/wiki/BBC_Four" title="BBC Four">BBC Four</a> on 19 December 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2015, 13STAR Records released a box set <i>1974-1979</i> by March 23 which included the studio albums <i>Mr. Natural</i>, <i>Main Course</i>, <i>Children of the World</i> and <i>Spirits Having Flown</i>. A fifth disc called <i>The Miami Years</i> includes all the tracks from <i>Saturday Night Fever</i> as well as B-Sides. No unreleased tracks from the era were included.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Influences">Influences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bee_Gees&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Influences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Bee Gees were influenced by <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">The Beatles</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Everly_Brothers" title="The Everly Brothers">The Everly Brothers</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Mills_Brothers" title="The Mills Brothers">The Mills Brothers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley" title="Elvis Presley">Elvis Presley</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Rolling_Stones" title="The Rolling Stones">The Rolling Stones</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brothers_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-brothers-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> On the 2014 documentary <i>The Joy of the Bee Gees</i>, Barry claimed that the Bee Gees were also influenced by <a href="/wiki/The_Hollies" title="The Hollies">the Hollies</a> and <a href="/wiki/Otis_Redding" title="Otis Redding">Otis Redding</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bee_Gees&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Brian_May" title="Brian May">Brian May</a> of <a href="/wiki/Queen_(band)" title="Queen (band)">Queen</a> said: "Of course I was, and am a huge fan of the Bee Gees' creations in music. Undoubtedly at the pinnacle of song-writing considered over the last—30 years, is it?! My fondest recollections are not of the SNF days, which were really a re-birth in the Bee Gees' popularity, but the early ground-breaking songs [...] I remember singing these [songs] with my pal Tim Staffell [of <a href="/wiki/Smile_(band)" title="Smile (band)">Smile</a>] and <a href="/wiki/Freddie_Mercury" title="Freddie Mercury">Freddie</a> [Mercury] in the real old days." May also praised the song "<a href="/wiki/You_Win_Again_(Bee_Gees_song)" title="You Win Again (Bee Gees song)">You Win Again</a>" as one of the greatest songs of the '80s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-greatest_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-greatest-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a>, who was also influenced by the Bee Gees says, "I cried listening to their music. I knew every note, every instrument". <a href="/wiki/Paul_McCartney" title="Paul McCartney">Paul McCartney</a> recalls "It was the '<a href="/wiki/New_York_Mining_Disaster_1941" title="New York Mining Disaster 1941">Mining Disaster</a>' song that <a href="/wiki/Robert_Stigwood" title="Robert Stigwood">Robert Stigwood</a> played me, I said 'sign them, they're great'". <a href="/wiki/Ringo_Starr" title="Ringo Starr">Ringo Starr</a> said, "The Bee Gees from our era were quite important, especially the harmonies."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-greatest_88-1"><a href="#cite_note-greatest-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> In a 2007 with Duane Hitchings, who co-wrote <a href="/wiki/Rod_Stewart" title="Rod Stewart">Rod Stewart</a>'s 1978 disco song "<a href="/wiki/Da_Ya_Think_I%27m_Sexy%3F" title="Da Ya Think I'm Sexy?">Da Ya Think I'm Sexy?</a>" noted that the song was:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-music_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-music-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>"a spoof on guys from the 'cocaine lounge lizards' of the <i><a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Fever" title="Saturday Night Fever">Saturday Night Fever</a></i> days. We Rock and Roll guys thought we were dead meat when that movie and the Bee Gees came out. The Bee Gees were brilliant musicians and really nice people. No big egos. Rod, in his brilliance, decided to do a spoof on disco. VERY smart man. There is no such thing as a "dumb" super success in the music business."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-music_89-1"><a href="#cite_note-music-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>Barry Gibb once said: "When we first came out, <a href="/wiki/Jimi_Hendrix" title="Jimi Hendrix">Jimi Hendrix</a> said we were two-year old <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">Beatles</a>. He was just giving an opinion at the time. People just like to have go at other artists. But we are very good friends with Jimi now". Years later, Gibb recalled: "He was a great mate of mine. He came to my twenty-first birthday. He was an extremely polite bloke. I never knew about the drugs then. I thought he was acting a bit weird and saying kind of remote things, but I was too naive to even consider that it might be drugs, I never caught on with Jimi and the drugs. I saw him drunk a few times because I remember thinking he was always really quiet until he had a few drinks". .<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-first_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-first-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> English <a href="/wiki/Indie_rock" title="Indie rock">indie rock</a> band <a href="/wiki/The_Cribs" title="The Cribs">the Cribs</a> was also influenced by the Bee Gees. Cribs member <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Jarman" title="Ryan Jarman">Ryan Jarman</a> said that "It must have had quite a big influence on us – pop melodies is something we always revert to. I always want to get back to pop melodies and I'm sure that's due to that Bee Gees phase we went through".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Following Robin's death in 20 May 2012, <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9" title="Beyoncé">Beyoncé</a> remarked: "The Bee Gees were an early inspiration for me, <a href="/wiki/Kelly_Rowland" title="Kelly Rowland">Kelly Rowland</a> and <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Michelle_Williams" title="Michelle Williams">Michelle</a>. We loved their songwriting and beautiful harmonies. Recording their classic song, 'Emotion' was a special time for Destiny’s Child. Sadly we lost Robin Gibb this week. My heart goes out to his brother Barry and the rest of his family.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> While <a href="/wiki/Justin_Bieber" title="Justin Bieber">Justin Bieber</a> told MTV: “I definitely listened to the Bee Gees". Singer <a href="/wiki/Jordin_Sparks" title="Jordin Sparks">Jordin Sparks</a> remarked that her favorite Bee Gees songs are "Too Much Heaven", "Emotion" (although performed by Samantha Sang with Barry on the background vocals using his falsetto) and "Stayin' Alive".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-falsetto_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-falsetto-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Carrie_Underwood" title="Carrie Underwood">Carrie Underwood</a>, on discovering the Bee Gees during her childhood, "My parents listened to the Bee Gees quite a bit when I was little, so I was definitely exposed to them at an early age. They just had a sound that was all their own, obviously, [it was] never duplicated".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-falsetto_93-1"><a href="#cite_note-falsetto-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Other artists who were influenced by the Bee Gees are <a href="/wiki/Pet_Shop_Boys" title="Pet Shop Boys">Pet Shop Boys</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Michael" title="George Michael">George Michael</a>, <a href="/wiki/Billy_Joel" title="Billy Joel">Billy Joel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Simon" title="Paul Simon">Paul Simon</a> of <a href="/wiki/Simon_%26_Garfunkel" title="Simon &amp; Garfunkel">Simon &amp; Garfunkel</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Bowie" title="David Bowie">David Bowie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brian_Wilson" title="Brian Wilson">Brian Wilson</a> of <a href="/wiki/The_Beach_Boys" title="The Beach Boys">The Beach Boys</a>, <a href="/wiki/Debbie_Harry" title="Debbie Harry">Debbie Harry</a> of <a href="/wiki/Blondie_(band)" title="Blondie (band)">Blondie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madonna_(entertainer)" title="Madonna (entertainer)">Madonna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andy_Bell_(musician)" title="Andy Bell (musician)">Andy Bell</a> of <a href="/wiki/Beady_Eye" title="Beady Eye">Beady Eye</a>, <a href="/wiki/Noel_Gallagher" title="Noel Gallagher">Noel Gallagher</a> and <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> The Bee Gees have sold in excess of 220 million records worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardianjuly13_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-Guardianjuly13-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Songwriting">Songwriting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bee_Gees&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Songwriting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Barry,_Robin_%26_Maurice_Gibb" title="Barry, Robin &amp; Maurice Gibb">Barry, Robin &amp; Maurice Gibb</a></div>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:28%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"Everyone should be aware that the Bee Gees are second only to Lennon and McCartney as the most successful songwriting unit in British popular music."</p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;">—Music historian <a href="/wiki/Paul_Gambaccini" title="Paul Gambaccini">Paul Gambaccini</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
<p>At one point in 1978, the Gibb brothers were responsible for writing and/or performing nine of the songs in the Billboard Hot 100.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> In all, the Gibbs placed 13 singles onto the Hot 100 in 1978, with 12 making the Top 40. The Gibb brothers are fellows of the <a href="/wiki/British_Academy_of_Songwriters,_Composers_and_Authors" title="British Academy of Songwriters, Composers and Authors">British Academy of Songwriters, Composers and Authors</a> (BASCA).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> At least 2,500 artists have recorded their songs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> Their most popular composition is "How Deep Is Your Love", with 400 versions by other artists in existence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Singer-songwriter <a href="/wiki/Gavin_DeGraw" title="Gavin DeGraw">Gavin DeGraw</a> spoke to the Bee Gees' influence with their own music as well as their songwriting:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>"Let’s talk about the Bee Gees. That’s an iconic group. Not just a great band, but a great group of songwriters. Even long after the Bee Gees' success on the pop charts, they were still writing songs for other people, huge hit songs. Their talent went far beyond their moment of normal pop success. It is a loss to the music industry and a loss of an iconic group. The beauty of this industry is that we do pay tribute and every artist coming up is a fan of a generation prior to it, so there’s a real tradition element to it".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-falsetto_93-2"><a href="#cite_note-falsetto-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>Among the artists who have covered their songs are <a href="/wiki/Michael_Bolton" title="Michael Bolton">Michael Bolton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boyzone" title="Boyzone">Boyzone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eric_Clapton" title="Eric Clapton">Eric Clapton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Billy_Corgan" title="Billy Corgan">Billy Corgan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Destiny%27s_Child" title="Destiny's Child">Destiny's Child</a>, <a href="/wiki/Faith_No_More" title="Faith No More">Faith No More</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Flaming_Lips" title="The Flaming Lips">The Flaming Lips</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Frusciante" title="John Frusciante">John Frusciante</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Green" title="Al Green">Al Green</a>, <a href="/wiki/Engelbert_Humperdinck_(singer)" title="Engelbert Humperdinck (singer)">Engelbert Humperdinck</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tom_Jones_(singer)" title="Tom Jones (singer)">Tom Jones</a>, <a href="/wiki/Janis_Joplin" title="Janis Joplin">Janis Joplin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lulu_(singer)" title="Lulu (singer)">Lulu</a>, <a href="/wiki/N-Trance" title="N-Trance">N-Trance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pet_Shop_Boys" title="Pet Shop Boys">Pet Shop Boys</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley" title="Elvis Presley">Elvis Presley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nina_Simone" title="Nina Simone">Nina Simone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Percy_Sledge" title="Percy Sledge">Percy Sledge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Smith_(musician)" title="Robert Smith (musician)">Robert Smith</a>, <a href="/wiki/Status_Quo_(band)" title="Status Quo (band)">Status Quo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steps_(group)" title="Steps (group)">Steps</a> and <a href="/wiki/Take_That" title="Take That">Take That</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_achievements">Awards and achievements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bee_Gees&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Awards and achievements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Walk-BG-1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1920" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Walk-BG-1.jpg/220px-Walk-BG-1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Walk-BG-1.jpg/330px-Walk-BG-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Walk-BG-1.jpg/440px-Walk-BG-1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Walk-BG-1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bee Gees' star on the <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame" title="Hollywood Walk of Fame">Hollywood Walk of Fame</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In October 1999 the Isle of Man Post Office unveiled a set of 6 stamps honouring their native sons' music. The official launch took place at the London Palladium where the stage show of <i><a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Fever_(musical)" title="Saturday Night Fever (musical)">Saturday Night Fever</a></i> was playing. A similar launch was held in New York shortly after to coincide with the show opening across the Atlantic. The songs depicted on the stamps are "Massachusetts", "Words", "I've Gotta Get A Message To You", "Night Fever", "Stayin' Alive" and "Immortality".</p>
<p>In 1978, following the success of <i>Saturday Night Fever</i>, and the single "Night Fever" in particular, <a href="/wiki/Reubin_Askew" title="Reubin Askew">Reubin Askew</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Governor_of_Florida" title="Governor of Florida">Governor</a> of the US state of Florida, named the Bee Gees honorary citizens of the state, since they resided in Miami at the time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1979, the Bee Gees got their star on the <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame" title="Hollywood Walk of Fame">Hollywood Walk of Fame</a>. They were inducted in 1994 on the <a href="/wiki/Songwriters_Hall_of_Fame" title="Songwriters Hall of Fame">Songwriters Hall of Fame</a>, as well as Florida's Artists Hall of Fame in 1995, ARIA Hall of Fame in 1997. Also in 1997, the Bee Gees were inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a>. In 2001, they were inducted on the Vocal Group Hall of Fame.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> After Maurice's death, the Bee Gees inducted in Dance Music Hall of Fame in 2001, London's Walk of Fame in 2006 and Musically Speaking Hall Of Fame in 2008. And on 15 May 2007, the Bee Gees were named <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Broadcast_Music_Incorporated" title="Broadcast Music Incorporated">BMI Icons</a> at the 55th annual BMI Pop Awards. Collectively, Barry, Maurice and Robin Gibb have earned 109 BMI Pop, Country and Latin Awards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>All three brothers (including Maurice, posthumously) were appointed Commanders in the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_British_Empire" title="Order of the British Empire">Order of the British Empire</a> in December 2001 with the ceremony taking place at <a href="/wiki/Buckingham_Palace" title="Buckingham Palace">Buckingham Palace</a> on 27 May 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> On 10 July 2009, the Isle of Man's capital bestowed the <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_the_City" title="Freedom of the City">Freedom of the Borough of Douglas</a> honour on Barry and Robin, as well as posthumously on Maurice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> On 20 November 2009, the Douglas Borough Council released a limited edition commemorative DVD to mark their naming as Freemen of the Borough.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 14 February 2013, Barry Gibb unveiled a statue of the Bee Gees, as well as unveiling "Bee Gees Way" (a walkway filled with photos of the Bee Gees), in honour of the Bee Gees in <a href="/wiki/Redcliffe,_Queensland" title="Redcliffe, Queensland">Redcliffe</a>, Queensland, Australia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Band_members">Band members</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bee_Gees&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Band members">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Barry Gibb played <a href="/wiki/Acoustic_guitar" title="Acoustic guitar">rhythm guitar</a>. During the early 1970s, Robin Gibb played <a href="/wiki/Piano" title="Piano">piano</a> and <a href="/wiki/Violin" title="Violin">violin</a> occasionally, after which, he only played strings and <a href="/wiki/Keyboard_instrument" title="Keyboard instrument">keyboards</a> privately. Maurice Gibb played <a href="/wiki/Bass_guitar" title="Bass guitar">bass guitar</a>, rhythm guitar, <a href="/wiki/Lead_guitar" title="Lead guitar">lead guitar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harmonica" title="Harmonica">harmonica</a>, piano, <a href="/wiki/Organ_(music)" title="Organ (music)">organ</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mellotron" title="Mellotron">mellotron</a>, keyboard, <a href="/wiki/Synthesizer" title="Synthesizer">synthesizer</a> and created <a href="/wiki/Drum_tracks" title="Drum tracks">drum tracks</a>. From 1966 to 1972 he played multiple instruments on many records. During the late 1970s he played mainly bass guitar. From about 1986 onward he usually played keyboards and guitars. Maurice was credited by the brothers as being the most technologically savvy member of the band.</p>
<dl>
<dt>Principal members</dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Barry_Gibb" title="Barry Gibb">Barry Gibb</a> – vocals, guitar <small>(1958–2012)</small></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Robin_Gibb" title="Robin Gibb">Robin Gibb</a> – vocals <small>(1958–69, 1970–2012; died 2012)</small></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Maurice_Gibb" title="Maurice Gibb">Maurice Gibb</a> – vocals, guitar, bass, keyboards <small>(1958–2003; died 2003)</small></li>
</ul>
<p>These musicians were considered members of the band:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Colin_Petersen" title="Colin Petersen">Colin Petersen</a> – drums <small>(1967–69)</small></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Vince_Melouney" title="Vince Melouney">Vince Melouney</a> – lead guitar <small>(1967–68)</small></li>
<li>Geoff Bridgford – drums <small>(1971–72)</small></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Discography">Discography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bee_Gees&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Discography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<p>See also the soundtracks <i><a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Fever_(soundtrack)" title="Saturday Night Fever (soundtrack)">Saturday Night Fever</a></i> (1977) and <i><a href="/wiki/Staying_Alive_(1983_film)#Soundtrack" title="Staying Alive (1983 film)">Staying Alive</a></i> (1983), which contain music not released on their original LPs. All their officially released LPs included on this list; <i><a href="/wiki/A_Kick_in_the_Head_Is_Worth_Eight_in_the_Pants" title="A Kick in the Head Is Worth Eight in the Pants">A Kick in the Head Is Worth Eight in the Pants</a></i> have not been included on the list because it only appeared on numerous bootlegs and was not officially released.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Song_catalogue">Song catalogue</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bee_Gees&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Song catalogue">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Gibbs recently gained ownership rights to their back catalogue, returning distribution rights to <a href="/wiki/Warner_Music_Group" title="Warner Music Group">Warner Music Group</a> (which had purchased Atco), where they have since reissued digitally remastered versions of <i>Saturday Night Fever</i>, their later <i>Bee Gees Greatest</i> album, and a new boxed set: <i>The Studio Albums: 1967–1968</i> under the <a href="/wiki/Reprise_Records" title="Reprise Records">Reprise Records</a>/<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rhino_Records" title="Rhino Records">Rhino Records</a> labels.</p>
<p>Additionally, more recent titles such as <i><a href="/wiki/Still_Waters_(Bee_Gees_album)" title="Still Waters (Bee Gees album)">Still Waters</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/This_Is_Where_I_Came_In" title="This Is Where I Came In">This Is Where I Came In</a></i> were among the first batch of re-releases. The band's three <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros." title="Warner Bros.">Warner Bros.</a> releases, <i>E. S. P.,</i> <i>One</i> and <i>High Civilisation</i> were also made available on iTunes for the first time since the albums went out of print in North America in the mid-90s. According to Robin Gibb's website, three more reissues were planned for the 2008 holiday season: <i><a href="/wiki/Best_of_Bee_Gees" title="Best of Bee Gees">Best of Bee Gees</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Best_of_Bee_Gees,_Volume_2" title="Best of Bee Gees, Volume 2">Best of Bee Gees, Volume 2</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Love_Songs_(Bee_Gees_album)" title="Love Songs (Bee Gees album)">Love Songs</a></i>. The double album <i><a href="/wiki/Odessa_(Bee_Gees_album)" title="Odessa (Bee Gees album)">Odessa</a></i> was released on 13 January 2009 in a special 3-disc deluxe edition complete with the original red velvet cover with remastered stereo and mono versions of the album as well as alternate versions and unreleased tracks.</p>
<p>Since the remastered release of <i>Odessa</i>, Rhino has stopped reissuing original Bee Gees albums and there has not been any announcement as to when the remaining albums will be remastered.</p>
<p><span lang="gv"><i><a href="/wiki/Ellan_Vannin_(poem)#The_Bee_Gees_Version" title="Ellan Vannin (poem)">Ellan Vannin</a></i></span> was recorded in 1997 as a 1,000 quantity limited edition single for <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man" title="Isle of Man">Isle of Man</a> charities. The song was featured in the Bee Gees World Tour and on <a href="/wiki/ITV_(TV_channel)" title="ITV (TV channel)">ITV</a>'s "An Evening With ..." but to date has not been released generally. The single was subsequently also available as part of the 1999 Bee Gees Stamp issue.</p>
<p>In conjunction with the 50th anniversary of the Bee Gees (when they started calling themselves "Bee Gees" in 1959), Rhino Records have released two new collections. <i><a href="/wiki/Mythology_(Bee_Gees_album)" title="Mythology (Bee Gees album)">Mythology</a></i> is a four-disc collection highlighting each brother, including Andy, with tracks personally selected by Barry, Robin, Maurice's wife Yvonne (with his children Adam and Samantha), and Andy's daughter Peta. Maurice's disc contains two unreleased tracks called "Angel of Mercy" and "The Bridge". Andy's disc contains the unreleased track "Arrow Through The Heart". <i>Mythology</i> also features a scrapbook of family photos, many never-before published, along with tributes from artists such as <a href="/wiki/George_Martin" title="George Martin">George Martin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brian_Wilson" title="Brian Wilson">Brian Wilson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a>, <a href="/wiki/Graham_Nash" title="Graham Nash">Graham Nash</a> and the band's longtime manager <a href="/wiki/Robert_Stigwood" title="Robert Stigwood">Robert Stigwood</a>.</p>
<p>The second collection, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Ultimate_Bee_Gees" title="The Ultimate Bee Gees">The Ultimate Bee Gees</a></i>, is a more modest two-disc 40-track collection highlighting their biggest hits and includes a bonus DVD of unreleased videos, previously unreleased television appearances, live performances, and promo videos. Each disc is themed, with the first disc being the more upbeat songs called "A Night Out" and the second disc being more ballad-focused called "A Night In".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
